At line 792, when -ERESTARTSYS is received, it calls rpc_exit(task, -ERESTARTSYS). This propagates the error back to the caller. So the RPC layer is correctly propagating the signal-induced error back to the NFS layer.\n\nThe problem is that the NFS layer is then treating this error as a permanent failure instead of a retryable error. Let me search for how NFS is supposed to handle -ERESTARTSYS.\n\nActually, I think the real issue is different. Let me re-read the bug report more carefully:\"tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.\"This suggests that the server DID reply successfully, but the client is returning an error anyway. This could happen if:1. The reply is received but not processed2. The task is killed after the reply is received but before it's processed\n3. There's a race condition in reply processing\n\nLet me search for the xprtrdma/xprtsock reply processing code. But first, let me think about what could cause this. The tcpdump shows the server replying without error, so the network is working. But the client returns -ERESTARTSYS, which suggests the task got interrupted after the reply came back.\n\nActually, looking at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code again at lines 34-42:```c\ndo {    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)        break;\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\nreturn res;\n```\n\nThe problem here is:1. Call rpc_call_sync\n2. If it returns -EJUKEBOX, wait for timeout\n3. Set res = -ERESTARTSYS (unconditionally!)\n\n\n4. Loop while no fatal signal pending\n\nWait, that's not right. The res = -ERESTARTSYS at line 39 should be AFTER checking for the fatal signal, not before. Or it should only be set if there's a fatal signal pending.\n\nLet me trace through this more carefully:1. res = rpc_call_sync() - returns some value\n2. if (res != -EJUKEBOX) break - if it's not JUKEBOX, exit the loop\n3. else freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() - wait for timeout (can be interrupted)\n4. res = -ERESTARTSYS - set error to ERESTARTSYS unconditionally after the sleep, then check if there's a fatal signal pending before looping again. This means even if the sleep completes normally without interruption, we're still setting the error code to ERESTARTSYS, which seems wrong.\n\nThe flow appears to be: retry the RPC call, and if it returns JUKEBOX, sleep for a bit (which can be interrupted by signals). After waking up, unconditionally mark the result as needing restart, then only continue looping if no fatal signal has arrived. This logic is confusing—why set ERESTARTSYS every iteration regardless of whether a signal actually interrupted the sleep?\n\nI suspect the real issue is that freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() might return early due to a signal, but the code still sets res to -ERESTARTSYS and returns it, even if the RPC call itself succeeded and its reply was already processed. This could explain why a valid response gets overwritten with an error code. The regression between kernel versions suggests something changed in how this retry mechanism or signal handling works. The RPC reply is being received by the server according to tcpdump, but the client isn't processing it correctly and returns an error instead. This points to an issue in how the RPC layer handles the incoming reply rather than the signal handling or retry {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01UNkD3X5c9eqGUDq26yCh1n","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"FOUND IT! This is the bug!\n\nLooking at the nfs3_rpc_wrapper code:\n\n```c\ndo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n        break;\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;  // <-- BUG! This line is unconditional\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\nreturn res;\n```\n\nThe bug is at line 39: `res = -ERESTARTSYS;`\n\nThis line unconditionally sets res to -ERESTARTSYS AFTER every freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe call, even if no signal interrupted the schedule!\n\nThe logic should be:\n1. Call rpc_call_sync\n2. If result is not -EJUKEBOX, return it\n3. If result is -EJUKEBOX, sleep for a timeout\n4. If the sleep was interrupted by a signal, return -ERESTARTSYS\n5. Otherwise, retry the call\n\nBut what's actually happening is:\n1. Call rpc_call_sync\n2. If result is not -EJUKEBOX, return it\n3. If result is -EJUKEBOX, sleep for a timeout\n4. ALWAYS set res = -ERESTARTSYS (regardless of whether we were actually interrupted)\n5. Loop while no fatal signal pending\n\nSo the sleep might complete normally, but res is still set to -ERESTARTSYS!\n\nThen the loop condition checks `while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))`. Since there might not be a fatal signal pending (the sleep just timed out), the loop continues and retries the call.\n\nBut wait, that means the loop would retry. Let me trace through this more carefully:\n\nIteration 1:\n- res = rpc_call_sync() returns -EJUKEBOX\n\n\n- res != -EJUKEBOX is false, so don't break\n- freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() sleeps (returns 0 if completed normally, -ERESTARTSYS if interrupted)\n- res = -ERESTARTSYS (unconditional assignment, BUG!)\n- Check while (!fatal_signal_pending(current))\n  - If no fatal signal, loop back\n  - If fatal signal, exit loop\n\nIf the loop goes back to iteration 2:\n- res = rpc_call_sync() is called again (because we're back at the top of the loop)\n\nThe core issue is that res gets overwritten with -ERESTARTSYS unconditionally after the sleep, regardless of whether the sleep actually completed or was interrupted. This means even a normal timeout completion gets treated as a signal interruption, causing the function to return -ERESTARTSYS when it should retry the RPC call instead. fatal signal is pending after the sleep? The loop exits with res = -ERESTARTSYS. If there's no fatal signal but the sleep gets interrupted by a non-fatal signal, the loop continues and retries the RPC call.\n\nThe logic appears sound for handling retries. The key insight is that `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe` will return early with -ERESTARTSYS if a fatal signal arrives, and then the loop condition prevents further iterations since the signal is now pending. For non-fatal interruptions, the loop continues as intended.\n\nHowever, there's a critical flaw: line 39 unconditionally overwrites `res` with -ERESTARTSYS regardless of what `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe` actually returned. When the sleep completes normally (returns 0), we should retry the RPC call, not immediately return an error. The current code loses this distinction between a normal timeout completion and an actual signal It returns:\n- 0 if the timeout completes normally\n- positive value if the timeout was interrupted (time remaining)\n- negative value potentially for errors\n\nThe key is that it returns a long value, not necessarily -ERESTARTSYS. So the code at line 39 that unconditionally sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS` is definitely wrong!\n\nIf the timeout completes normally (returns 0), we should retry the RPC call, not return -ERESTARTSYS.\nIf the timeout is interrupted (returns non-zero), we should check if it's a fatal signal before returning -ERESTARTSYS.\n\nThe fix should be:\n```c\ndo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n (!fatal_signal_pending(current) && res != -ERESTARTSYS);\nreturn res;\n```\n\nOr more simply:\n```cdo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)        break;\n {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01NacwQNDA9fnTh1nq9hFCdV","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I've confirmed the bug. The code at line 39 unconditionally sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS` after every `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe` call. This is the bug that causes NFS getattr calls to return -512 (-ERESTARTSYS) even when the server has already replied successfully.\n\nThe problem is that:\n1. Line 35: rpc_call_sync is called\n2. Line 36-37: If it returns -EJUKEBOX, don't break\n3. Line 38: Sleep for JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME (this might complete normally)\n4. Line 39: UNCONDITIONALLY set res = -ERESTARTSYS (BUG!)\n5. Line 40: Loop while no fatal signal pending\n\nThe issue is that line 39 doesn't check whether the sleep was actually interrupted. It just unconditionally sets the result to -ERESTARTSYS. This means that even if:\n- The sleep completed normally (timeout expired)\n- No signal interrupted it\n- The result was previously a successful RPC reply\n\nThe function will still return -ERESTARTSYS.\n\nThis causes the inode revalidation to fail with -ERESTARTSYS, which is then treated as a permanent failure by nfs_lookup_revalidate, leading to the entire directory cache being Here's a summary of my findings:\n\n## Bug Analysis Summary\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`, function `nfs3_rpc_wrapper()`, line 39\n\n**The Bug**: The function unconditionally sets `res = -ERESTARTSYS` after every `freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe()` call, regardless of whether the sleep was actually interrupted by a signal or completed normally.\n\n**Root Cause**: \n```c\ndo {\n    res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n    if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n        break;\n    freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n    res = -ERESTARTSYS;  // <-- BUG! Unconditional assignment\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n```\n\n**Impact**:\n1. When a getattr RPC call encounters -EJUKEBOX, the code sleeps and then returns `-512` (-ERESTARTSYS) even if the sleep completed normally without signal interruption\n2. This -ERESTARTSYS propagates to `nfs_lookup_revalidate()` \n3. Any non-zero error from `nfs_lookup_verify_inode()` triggers `out_zap_parent`, which invalidates the entire directory cache\n4. For autofs mounts, this causes the entire mount point to be unmounted, not just the NFS volume\n\n**Why it's a regression**: The code should only return -ERESTARTSYS when a fatal signal actually interrupts the sleep, not unconditionally.
